[2025-05-17 15:57:55,875] INFO: Here’s a small Unity C# script that will automatically add the five missing primitives under a “Classroom” root. Drop this into your Assets/Scripts folder, attach it to any GameObject in your scene (or an empty GameObject), then hit Play to populate the walls and floor exactly as specified:

```csharp
using UnityEngine;

public class ClassroomBuilder : MonoBehaviour
{
    void Start()
    {
        // Find or create the Classroom parent object
        Transform classroom = GameObject.Find("Classroom")?.transform;
        if (classroom == null)
            classroom = new GameObject("Classroom").transform;

        // Front Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Front",
            localPosition: new Vector3(0f, 1.5f, 4f),
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Back Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Back",
            localPosition: new Vector3(0f, 1.5f, -4f),
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Left Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Left",
            localPosition: new Vector3(-5f, 1.5f, 0f),
            localEuler:   new Vector3(0f, 90f, 0f),
            localScale:   new Vector3(8f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Right Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Right",
            localPosition: new Vector3(5f, 1.5f, 0f),
            localEuler:   new Vector3(0f, 90f, 0f),
            localScale:   new Vector3(8f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Floor
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Floor",
            localPosition: Vector3.zero,
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 1f, 8f)
        );
    }

    private void CreatePrimitiveCube(Transform parent, string name, Vector3 localPosition, Vector3 localEuler, Vector3 localScale)
    {
        var go = GameObject.CreatePrimitive(PrimitiveType.Cube);
        go.name = name;
        go.transform.parent = parent;
        go.transform.localPosition = localPosition;
        go.transform.localEulerAngles = localEuler;
        go.transform.localScale = localScale;
    }
}
```

What this does  
- Looks for a root GameObject called “Classroom” (creates it if not found).  
- Adds each wall/floor as a Cube primitive, sets the name, position, rotation, and scale exactly as per your suggested fixes  

After running, you’ll see:  
• Wall_Front at (0,1.5,4) size (10×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Back at (0,1.5,-4) size (10×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Left at (−5,1.5,0) rotated 90° Y, size (8×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Right at (5,1.5,0) rotated 90° Y, size (8×3×0.2)  
• Floor at (0,0,0) size (10×1×8)  

You can now continue adding desks, chairs, and all the other items per your action plan.

[2025-05-17 15:58:31,648] INFO: Input scene:  Here’s a small Unity C# script that will automatically add the five missing primitives under a “Classroom” root. Drop this into your Assets/Scripts folder, attach it to any GameObject in your scene (or an empty GameObject), then hit Play to populate the walls and floor exactly as specified:

```csharp
using UnityEngine;

public class ClassroomBuilder : MonoBehaviour
{
    void Start()
    {
        // Find or create the Classroom parent object
        Transform classroom = GameObject.Find("Classroom")?.transform;
        if (classroom == null)
            classroom = new GameObject("Classroom").transform;

        // Front Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Front",
            localPosition: new Vector3(0f, 1.5f, 4f),
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Back Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Back",
            localPosition: new Vector3(0f, 1.5f, -4f),
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Left Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Left",
            localPosition: new Vector3(-5f, 1.5f, 0f),
            localEuler:   new Vector3(0f, 90f, 0f),
            localScale:   new Vector3(8f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Right Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Right",
            localPosition: new Vector3(5f, 1.5f, 0f),
            localEuler:   new Vector3(0f, 90f, 0f),
            localScale:   new Vector3(8f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Floor
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Floor",
            localPosition: Vector3.zero,
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 1f, 8f)
        );
    }

    private void CreatePrimitiveCube(Transform parent, string name, Vector3 localPosition, Vector3 localEuler, Vector3 localScale)
    {
        var go = GameObject.CreatePrimitive(PrimitiveType.Cube);
        go.name = name;
        go.transform.parent = parent;
        go.transform.localPosition = localPosition;
        go.transform.localEulerAngles = localEuler;
        go.transform.localScale = localScale;
    }
}
```

What this does  
- Looks for a root GameObject called “Classroom” (creates it if not found).  
- Adds each wall/floor as a Cube primitive, sets the name, position, rotation, and scale exactly as per your suggested fixes  

After running, you’ll see:  
• Wall_Front at (0,1.5,4) size (10×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Back at (0,1.5,-4) size (10×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Left at (−5,1.5,0) rotated 90° Y, size (8×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Right at (5,1.5,0) rotated 90° Y, size (8×3×0.2)  
• Floor at (0,0,0) size (10×1×8)  

You can now continue adding desks, chairs, and all the other items per your action plan.

[2025-05-17 16:00:06,130] INFO: Input scene:  Here’s a small Unity C# script that will automatically add the five missing primitives under a “Classroom” root. Drop this into your Assets/Scripts folder, attach it to any GameObject in your scene (or an empty GameObject), then hit Play to populate the walls and floor exactly as specified:

```csharp
using UnityEngine;

public class ClassroomBuilder : MonoBehaviour
{
    void Start()
    {
        // Find or create the Classroom parent object
        Transform classroom = GameObject.Find("Classroom")?.transform;
        if (classroom == null)
            classroom = new GameObject("Classroom").transform;

        // Front Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Front",
            localPosition: new Vector3(0f, 1.5f, 4f),
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Back Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Back",
            localPosition: new Vector3(0f, 1.5f, -4f),
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Left Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Left",
            localPosition: new Vector3(-5f, 1.5f, 0f),
            localEuler:   new Vector3(0f, 90f, 0f),
            localScale:   new Vector3(8f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Right Wall
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Wall_Right",
            localPosition: new Vector3(5f, 1.5f, 0f),
            localEuler:   new Vector3(0f, 90f, 0f),
            localScale:   new Vector3(8f, 3f, 0.2f)
        );

        // Floor
        CreatePrimitiveCube(
            parent: classroom,
            name: "Floor",
            localPosition: Vector3.zero,
            localEuler:   Vector3.zero,
            localScale:   new Vector3(10f, 1f, 8f)
        );
    }

    private void CreatePrimitiveCube(Transform parent, string name, Vector3 localPosition, Vector3 localEuler, Vector3 localScale)
    {
        var go = GameObject.CreatePrimitive(PrimitiveType.Cube);
        go.name = name;
        go.transform.parent = parent;
        go.transform.localPosition = localPosition;
        go.transform.localEulerAngles = localEuler;
        go.transform.localScale = localScale;
    }
}
```

What this does  
- Looks for a root GameObject called “Classroom” (creates it if not found).  
- Adds each wall/floor as a Cube primitive, sets the name, position, rotation, and scale exactly as per your suggested fixes  

After running, you’ll see:  
• Wall_Front at (0,1.5,4) size (10×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Back at (0,1.5,-4) size (10×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Left at (−5,1.5,0) rotated 90° Y, size (8×3×0.2)  
• Wall_Right at (5,1.5,0) rotated 90° Y, size (8×3×0.2)  
• Floor at (0,0,0) size (10×1×8)  

You can now continue adding desks, chairs, and all the other items per your action plan.

[2025-05-17 16:00:54,395] INFO: Below is a single, self‐contained C# script you can drop into Assets/Scripts, attach to an empty GameObject (or your existing “Classroom” root), then hit Play. It will:

1. Adjust your 4 walls and floor per the collision fixes.  
2. Add all 20 student desks & chairs, teacher desk & chair, blackboard, projector, bookshelf, wall clock, potted plant, ceiling lights, posters, waste-bins, window and curtains exactly as specified.

```csharp
using UnityEngine;

public class ClassroomBuilder : MonoBehaviour
{
    void Start()
    {
        // Find or create the Classroom parent object
        Transform classroom = GameObject.Find("Classroom")?.transform;
        if (classroom == null)
            classroom = new GameObject("Classroom").transform;

        // --- 1) Walls & Floor (fixed positions/scales) ---
        CreateCube("Wall_Front",  classroom, new Vector3( 0f, 2.0f,  4f), Vector3.zero,           new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f));
        CreateCube("Wall_Back",   classroom, new Vector3( 0f, 2.0f, -4f), Vector3.zero,           new Vector3(10f, 3f, 0.2f));
        CreateCube("Wall_Left",   classroom, new Vector3(-5f, 2.0f,  0f), new Vector3(0,90,0),      new Vector3( 8f, 3f, 0.2f));
        CreateCube("Wall_Right",  classroom, new Vector3( 5f, 2.0f,  0f), new Vector3(0,90,0),      new Vector3( 8f, 3f, 0.2f));
        CreateCube("Floor",       classroom, new Vector3( 0f, 0.05f, 0f), Vector3.zero,           new Vector3(10f, 0.1f, 8f));

        // --- 2) Student desks & chairs (4 rows × 5 columns) ---
        for (int r = 1; r <= 4; r++)
        {
            for (int c = 1; c <= 5; c++)
            {
                float x = -4f + 2f * (c - 1);
                float z =  2f - 0.67f * (r - 1);

                // Desk
                string deskName  = $"StudentDesk_Row{r}_Col{c}";
                CreateCube(deskName, classroom,
                           new Vector3(x, 0.375f, z),
                           Vector3.zero,
                           new Vector3(1.5f, 0.75f, 0.75f));

                // Chair (behind desk, facing front)
                string chairName = $"StudentChair_Row{r}_Col{c}";
                CreateCube(chairName, classroom,
                           new Vector3(x, 0.25f, z - 0.5f),
                           new Vector3(0,180,0),
                           new Vector3(0.5f, 0.5f, 0.5f));
            }
        }

        // --- 3) Teacher desk & chair ---
        CreateCube("TeacherDesk", classroom,
                   new Vector3(0f, 0.375f, 3.5f),
                   Vector3.zero,
                   new Vector3(2f, 0.75f, 1f));

        CreateCube("TeacherChair", classroom,
                   new Vector3(0f, 0.375f, 3.0f),
                   new Vector3(0,180,0),
                   new Vector3(0.75f, 0.75f, 0.75f));

        // --- 4) Blackboard ---
        CreateCube("Blackboard", classroom,
                   new Vector3(0f, 2.25f, 3.9f),
                   Vector3.zero,
                   new Vector3(8f, 1.5f, 0.1f));

        // --- 5) Projector (ceiling) ---
        CreateCube("Projector", classroom,
                   new Vector3(0f, 2.9f, 3.5f),
                   Vector3.zero,
                   new Vector3(0.3f, 0.3f, 0.3f));

        // --- 6) Bookshelf on right wall ---
        CreateCube("Bookshelf", classroom,
                   new Vector3(4.65f, 1.5f, 0f),
                   new Vector3(0,90,0),
                   new Vector3(1f, 3f, 0.5f));

        // --- 7) Wall clock on left wall ---
        CreateCube("WallClock", classroom,
                   new Vector3(-4.85f, 2.5f, 0f),
                   new Vector3(0,90,0),
                   new Vector3(0.5f, 0.5f, 0.1f));

        // --- 8) Potted plant in back-left corner ---
        CreateCube("PottedPlant", classroom,
                   new Vector3(-4.5f, 0.3f, -3.5f),
                   new Vector3(0, -45, 0),
                   new Vector3(0.5f, 0.6f, 0.5f));

        // --- 9) Ceiling lights (4) ---
        Vector3[] lightPositions = {
            new Vector3(-2.5f, 2.9f, -1f),
            new Vector3( 2.5f, 2.9f, -1f),
            new Vector3(-2.5f, 2.9f,  1f),
            new Vector3( 2.5f, 2.9f,  1f),
        };
        for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++)
        {
            CreateCube($"CeilingLight_{i+1}", classroom,
                       lightPositions[i],
                       Vector3.zero,
                       new Vector3(0.2f, 0.2f, 0.2f));
        }

        // --- 10) Educational posters (6) ---
        //   4 on back wall
        float[] backXs = { -3f, -1f, 1f, 3f };
        foreach (float bx in backXs)
        {
            CreateCube($"Poster_Back_{bx}", classroom,
                       new Vector3(bx, 1.5f, -3.9f),
                       new Vector3(0,180,0),
                       new Vector3(1f, 1f, 0.05f));
        }
        //   2 on left wall
        float[] leftZs = {  2f, -2f };
        for (int i = 0; i < leftZs.Length; i++)
        {
            CreateCube($"Poster_Left_{i+1}", classroom,
                       new Vector3(-4.9f, 1.5f, leftZs[i]),
                       new Vector3(0,90,0),
                       new Vector3(1f, 1f, 0.05f));
        }

        // --- 11) Waste bins ---
        CreateCube("WasteBin_Teacher", classroom,
                   new Vector3(1.5f, 0.25f, 3.5f),
                   Vector3.zero,
                   new Vector3(0.3f, 0.5f, 0.3f));
        CreateCube("WasteBin_Back", classroom,
                   new Vector3(4.5f, 0.25f, -3.5f),
                   Vector3.zero,
                   new Vector3(0.3f, 0.5f, 0.3f));

        // --- 12) Window & Curtains on left wall ---
        CreateCube("Window", classroom,
                   new Vector3(-4.9f, 1.5f, 0f),
                   new Vector3(0,90,0),
                   new Vector3(3f, 2f, 0.1f));

        CreateCube("Curtain_Left", classroom,
                   new Vector3(-4.85f, 1.5f,  0.55f),
                   new Vector3(0,90,0),
                   new Vector3(1.5f, 2f, 0.05f));
        CreateCube("Curtain_Right", classroom,
                   new Vector3(-4.85f, 1.5f, -0.55f),
                   new Vector3(0,90,0),
                   new Vector3(1.5f, 2f, 0.05f));
    }

    // Helper: create a cube primitive under parent
    private void CreateCube(string name, Transform parent, Vector3 localPos, Vector3 localEuler, Vector3 localScale)
    {
        GameObject go = GameObject.CreatePrimitive(PrimitiveType.Cube);
        go.name = name;
        go.transform.SetParent(parent, false);
        go.transform.localPosition     = localPos;
        go.transform.localEulerAngles  = localEuler;
        go.transform.localScale        = localScale;
    }
}
```

How it works  
• It first finds (or makes) a `Classroom` GameObject.  
• It **adjusts** your four walls/floor to avoid intersection (per the issue-report fixes).  
• Then in sequence it **creates** all desks, chairs, teacher station, board, lights, posters, bins, window/curtains, etc., with the exact sizes, positions, and rotations you requested.  

Drop this script in, attach it, press Play, and your scene will be fully populated per the action plan and issue-report fixes.
